## Section 001: Tauri Executable Playbook Templates
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme but never states that its subject is a spec-first work-packet discipline that turns vague desktop requests into REQ-TAURI contracts, layered designs, and test plans
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a Tauri change crosses at least three trust boundaries, the webview frontend, the IPC command layer, and the Rust core, and untyped requests sail through compilation while failing at exactly those boundaries
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the request is a one-line prototype spike where packet ceremony costs more than the code, the work is pure frontend styling that never crosses IPC, or requirements churn so fast the contracts are stale before red
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference governs spec and planning discipline for Tauri desktop work and does not by itself teach Tauri APIs, prescribe UI frameworks, or authorize changes to capability files without review
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state up front that the theme is spec-first work-packet discipline for desktop features crossing webview, IPC, and Rust boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a template's value is realized at the boundary crossings it forces the author to name; a packet that never mentions windows, permissions, or IPC shapes has not yet engaged with Tauri at all
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to open the local specs playbook first and produce a work packet with requirement contracts, a frontend-to-Rust design scaffold, and a verification matrix before writing application code
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because a Tauri change crosses at least three trust boundaries, the webview frontend, the IPC command layer, and the Rust core, and untyped requests sail through compilation while failing at exactly those boundaries
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the request is a one-line prototype spike where packet ceremony costs more than the code, the work is pure frontend styling that never crosses IPC, or requirements churn so fast the contracts are stale before red
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference governs spec and planning discipline for Tauri desktop work and does not by itself teach Tauri APIs, prescribe UI frameworks, or authorize changes to capability files without review
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: state up front that the theme is spec-first work-packet discipline for desktop features crossing webview, IPC, and Rust boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies a template's value is realized at the boundary crossings it forces the author to name; a packet that never mentions windows, permissions, or IPC shapes has not yet engaged with Tauri at all
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the task is a desktop feature with a describable trigger and observable behavior, the team can name windows and permissions involved, and at least one test type can exercise the crossing from frontend to Rust
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because a Tauri change crosses at least three trust boundaries, the webview frontend, the IPC command layer, and the Rust core, and untyped requests sail through compilation while failing at exactly those boundaries
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where the request is a one-line prototype spike where packet ceremony costs more than the code, the work is pure frontend styling that never crosses IPC, or requirements churn so fast the contracts are stale before red
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by this reference governs spec and planning discipline for Tauri desktop work and does not by itself teach Tauri APIs, prescribe UI frameworks, or authorize changes to capability files without review
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the task is a desktop feature with a describable trigger and observable behavior, the team can name windows and permissions involved, and at least one test type can exercise the crossing from frontend to Rust
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that a template's value is realized at the boundary crossings it forces the author to name; a packet that never mentions windows, permissions, or IPC shapes has not yet engaged with Tauri at all
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: the request is a one-line prototype spike where packet ceremony costs more than the code, the work is pure frontend styling that never crosses IPC, or requirements churn so fast the contracts are stale before red
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are packet templates can be filled ritually with untestable prose, requirement IDs can drift from the tests that claim them, and a beautiful design scaffold can hide that nobody validated the permission set
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the task is a desktop feature with a describable trigger and observable behavior, the team can name windows and permissions involved, and at least one test type can exercise the crossing from frontend to Rust
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using this reference governs spec and planning discipline for Tauri desktop work and does not by itself teach Tauri APIs, prescribe UI frameworks, or authorize changes to capability files without review
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: code-first exploration for throwaway spikes, a lightweight checklist for frontend-only changes, or full architecture review with security sign-off when capabilities and sidecars change
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: how much packet ceremony is worth paying for small tasks is a judgment call the playbook does not quantify, so teams must tune the threshold from their own defect history
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: code-first exploration for throwaway spikes, a lightweight checklist for frontend-only changes, or full architecture review with security sign-off when capabilities and sidecars change
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare those alternatives against the decision to determine when a Tauri task must be converted into executable requirement contracts, a layered design plan, and a verification matrix before any implementation begins
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: alternatives become option theater when packet templates can be filled ritually with untestable prose, requirement IDs can drift from the tests that claim them, and a beautiful design scaffold can hide that nobody validated the permission set
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: compare only choices allowed by this reference governs spec and planning discipline for Tauri desktop work and does not by itself teach Tauri APIs, prescribe UI frameworks, or authorize changes to capability files without review
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: revise the guidance to contrast the default with each viable recovery and apply this section-specific change: state up front that the theme is spec-first work-packet discipline for desktop features crossing webview, IPC, and Rust boundaries
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Tauri Executable Playbook Templates", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: make the tradeoff consequential by connecting it to a template's value is realized at the boundary crossings it forces the author to name; a packet that never mentions windows, permissions, or IPC shapes has not yet engaged with Tauri at all

Bad: a packet whose only requirement says the app should work reliably. Borderline: skipping the packet for a spike but writing contracts before the spike is promoted

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed map lists one local playbook and three public URLs with equal factual labels, without recording that only the local file was read or which claims each external link could actually support
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every template, contract form, and loop this reference teaches is traceable to the single local playbook, while nothing in this corpus records a retrieval of the three public pages at any date
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the external rows are cited as current facts, the single local source is treated as an ecosystem consensus, or a claim about permissions or IPC is attributed to a page nobody opened
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the map assigns provenance for this document's claims and cannot certify that Tauri 2 APIs, capability schemas, or release practices still match what the local playbook assumed when written
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to mark the three external rows as unrefreshed candidates and record that the local playbook is the only read source
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a source map with one read source is a provenance ledger, not a triangulation; its honest job is to say so before an agent treats convergence as evidence

- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat the local specs playbook as the sole verified source for templates and process, and hold the Tauri docs, Tauri repository, and Rust API guidelines as unrefreshed candidates until a claim is checked against them

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists three corpus-hygiene failures but omits the desktop-specific anti-patterns the playbook itself campaigns against, vague untestable requirements, fat command layers, over-broad capabilities, and lifecycle behavior left as an afterthought
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because anti-patterns pay off during review triage, and a reviewer armed only with hygiene failures will approve a packet whose requirements are untestable and whose capability set grants the whole filesystem
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rows describe failures too abstractly to match a live diff, the replacement pattern is just the failure negated, or the registry grows unpruned until reviewers skim past it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry covers planning and spec failures for this theme and does not enumerate Rust language anti-patterns or frontend framework misuse, which belong to their own references
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add desktop-specific anti-pattern rows for vague requirements, fat commands, over-broad capabilities, sidecar neglect, and untested lifecycle

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names a single repository verifier for editing this file and is silent about the quality gates the playbook demands for actual Tauri work, fmt, clippy, Rust tests, Rust build, frontend checks, and tauri checks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a gate section that verifies only the documentation trains agents to treat green markdown as green software, while the playbook's packet template reserves explicit lines for each quality gate result precisely to prevent that substitution
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: gates are run selectively and only passing results recorded, a green build is read as requirement satisfaction, or the gate list drifts from the commands the repository actually supports
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: gates verify process and code health for this theme's work and do not replace the verification matrix, which maps individual requirements to individual tests
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the playbook's six quality gates with recording obligations alongside the document verifier
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that gates define what completion means; any gate left implicit will be satisfied implicitly, which is to say not at all

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table keys adopt, adapt, and avoid to generic local-versus-external evidence agreement rather than to the task properties that actually govern the choice, boundary crossings, permission changes, and requirement stability
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the cost of skipping contracts scales with the number of trust boundaries a change crosses, so boundary count and permission impact predict the value of the discipline far better than whether two document sets agree
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adopt is chosen because sources agree while the task is a spike, adapt quietly drops the verification matrix that was the point, or avoid becomes the habitual route for work that ships to users

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed hierarchy crowns one playbook canonical while its own confidence warning admits single-source thinness, and its reviewer question is a generic contribution prompt no single-row table needs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because hierarchy semantics assume competition, and with one row the real question is not ranking but calibration, how far one author's workflow choices should bind future agents without independent confirmation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: provisional canon quietly becomes permanent policy, the confidence warning is dropped in reuse, or a future second source is auto-ranked below the incumbent out of habit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the hierarchy classifies retrieval priority within this corpus and does not measure the playbook's quality against external Tauri practice, which the research map governs

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed metrics name one leading indicator and one failure signal but define no measurement owner, no run population, and no corrective action bound to any threshold
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because signals form a feedback loop only when a measurement on a defined population is wired to a corrective action; unattached indicators decay into slogans quoted in retrospectives
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: indicators are averaged across unlike tasks, the failure signal fires only after a release, cadence becomes calendar ritual detached from change events, or breaches accumulate with no revision ever applied
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: these metrics evaluate the reference and its planning discipline, not application performance or team velocity, which need their own instruments

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checklist verifies that sections exist and name things but never asks whether the guidance is internally consistent, executable by an agent, or faithful to the playbook it summarizes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because existence checks catch missing prose cheaply, but the expensive failures are contradictions between sections and gates that cannot run, which only content-level checks with citations intercept
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: items are ticked from memory without citations, a structural pass is read as content endorsement, or the checklist freezes while sections evolve and silently stops covering new obligations
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the checklist gates this document's readiness and does not certify outcomes of tasks that later use it, which the metrics section observes
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to append consistency, executability, fidelity, and capability-currency items and require cited evidence for every tick

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model states a one-crate, hundred-symbol, single-integration-path boundary inherited from generic Rust guidance and truncates its own heading-signal cell, without deriving any limit from what actually binds Tauri planning, contract count and cross-layer review
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the binding constraint is review comprehension across the six design layers, because each added contract multiplies matrix rows and gate surface faster than code volume grows
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: symbol counts are honored while a single capability change fans out across every window, the truncated source-pressure row is copied forward as noise, or slice limits are read as quality guarantees
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds one planning slice in one workspace and says nothing about team-level scheduling or multi-app release coordination
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rederive boundaries from contract count and layer spread, and repair the truncated heading-signal cell
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that Tauri work scales by boundaries crossed, not lines written; a workload model that counts symbols will approve exactly the permission-wide changes it should have split

- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to size slices by contract count and boundary spread, a handful of REQ-TAURI contracts whose design decisions and matrix rows one reviewer can hold at once, splitting when contracts multiply or a change spans several windows and capability files

- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: rederive boundaries from contract count and layer spread, and repair the truncated heading-signal cell
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies Tauri work scales by boundaries crossed, not lines written; a workload model that counts symbols will approve exactly the permission-wide changes it should have split

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table promises a 100 percent boundary-preservation rate and an 18-of-20 routing accuracy without any sampling procedure, sample source, or measurement owner in existence
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because targets create reliability only when someone can actually run the measurement; unmeasurable precision teaches readers to treat every number in the file as decoration
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: percentages are quoted as achievements rather than aspirations, samples are drawn only from successful tasks, misses trigger no correction, or the zero-unsupported-claim rule quietly exempts this very table
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the targets judge this document's guidance quality, not the reliability of Tauri itself or of applications built with it
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to attach a sampling procedure, population, owner, and miss-triggered action to each target and mark all thresholds unbaselined

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table pairs two corpus-hygiene rows with two systems rows on runtime contention and panic paths, but omits the desktop failure classes this theme's own sections rank highest, permission misscoping, IPC contract drift, and unowned lifecycle behavior
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because failure tables pay off at triage, and triage needs the failures that actually occur at webview, IPC, and packaging boundaries, ranked by blast radius in shipped binaries rather than by genericity
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rows describe failures too abstractly to match live symptoms, mitigations restate the failure as an imperative, or detection lands after packaging where evidence is expensive to gather
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table covers planning and boundary failures for this theme and cannot enumerate application-domain defects, which belong to each repository's own test regime
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add capability, IPC-drift, sidecar, and lifecycle rows with earliest-signal and detection-stage columns
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that a failure table that omits the failures its own theme exists to prevent leaves agents triaging desktop incidents with a generic map

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify failure causes and cap retries sensibly but never define who classifies, where classifications are recorded, or how a halt releases once the blocking gate recovers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retries without recorded classification become loops with amnesia, and implementing against red gates multiplies unverifiable work faster than review can absorb it
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a true contract contradiction is retried as if transient, a halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retry of planning and verification steps, not application-level retry logic inside the Tauri code being written, which belongs in requirement contracts
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add classification ownership, journal recording, and an evidence-based halt-release condition to the existing rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that backpressure is a memory discipline as much as flow control; a halt that does not record its cause converts recoverable congestion into permanent context loss
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify each failure once in the task record, allow one bounded retry only for transient or stale-evidence causes, halt new implementation while any quality gate is red, and resume only after the blocking evidence is recorded green
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because retries without recorded classification become loops with amnesia, and implementing against red gates multiplies unverifiable work faster than review can absorb it
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a true contract contradiction is retried as if transient, a halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this governs retry of planning and verification steps, not application-level retry logic inside the Tauri code being written, which belongs in requirement contracts
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add classification ownership, journal recording, and an evidence-based halt-release condition to the existing rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies backpressure is a memory discipline as much as flow control; a halt that does not record its cause converts recoverable congestion into permanent context loss
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: the guidance assumes recorded task journals, gates that report red or green unambiguously, and an agent empowered to pause its own implementation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because retries without recorded classification become loops with amnesia, and implementing against red gates multiplies unverifiable work faster than review can absorb it
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where a true contract contradiction is retried as if transient, a halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by this governs retry of planning and verification steps, not application-level retry logic inside the Tauri code being written, which belongs in requirement contracts
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in the guidance assumes recorded task journals, gates that report red or green unambiguously, and an agent empowered to pause its own implementation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that backpressure is a memory discipline as much as flow control; a halt that does not record its cause converts recoverable congestion into permanent context loss
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: a true contract contradiction is retried as if transient, a halt lifts because time passed rather than because evidence changed, or escalation has no named recipient
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are transient and systematic failures look identical on first occurrence, and rerunning a failed gate unchanged mostly reproduces the failure while consuming the retry budget
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the guidance assumes recorded task journals, gates that report red or green unambiguously, and an agent empowered to pause its own implementation

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: escalate immediately for authority or requirement-contradiction failures instead of consuming the retry, amend the input before any rerun, or hand persistent blockers to a fresh session through the journal
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: the right retry budget for semantic failures like weak contracts is judgment; one bounded retry is a defensible default, not a derived optimum

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets say record sources, commands, latencies, and error counters but never state where records live, which journey stage writes them, or who consumes each signal
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because evidence captured at the stage that produced it stays accurate and cheap, while end-of-session reconstruction forgets skipped sources and flattens the decision path into a tidy story
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: records are written only after success, latency percentiles are quoted for planning work nobody timed, or signals accumulate that no reviewer ever consumes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: observability here serves planning reconstruction and review, not runtime telemetry of the shipped desktop app, which the contracts themselves must specify
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to bind each recorded signal to a journey stage, storage location, and named consumer, and drop untimed latency claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that observability that depends on discipline fails under pressure; whatever the workflow does not capture structurally will be missing on exactly the runs worth investigating
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to write observations into the work packet at fixed stages, sources and skips at load, contracts and layer decisions at design, matrix and gate results at verification, and a compact completion audit naming unresolved risks at the end
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because evidence captured at the stage that produced it stays accurate and cheap, while end-of-session reconstruction forgets skipped sources and flattens the decision path into a tidy story
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; records are written only after success, latency percentiles are quoted for planning work nobody timed, or signals accumulate that no reviewer ever consumes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: observability here serves planning reconstruction and review, not runtime telemetry of the shipped desktop app, which the contracts themselves must specify
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: bind each recorded signal to a journey stage, storage location, and named consumer, and drop untimed latency claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies observability that depends on discipline fails under pressure; whatever the workflow does not capture structurally will be missing on exactly the runs worth investigating
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method demands memory, panic, and concurrency evidence with a 10 ms hot-path bound, importing runtime benchmarks into a planning document whose own pass condition is reviewer comprehension
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a reference performs by changing decisions, so its verification must compare decisions made with and without it rather than timing operations the document never performs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: percentile theater replaces judgment, pass is declared because a reviewer liked the prose, or comparison runs differ in task difficulty so the delta is noise
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this method evaluates the document's usefulness and does not benchmark Tauri runtime performance, which belongs inside REQ-TAURI contracts with explicit units
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recenter measurement on decision-quality comparison and move runtime bounds into the requirement contracts where they belong
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that measuring a planning document with runtime metrics is a category error that crowds out the harder measurement of whether it changes decisions

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement names multi-system spans, ownership boundaries, and SLO-bearing traffic as limits but gives no early indicators that a Tauri effort is approaching them before quality fails
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because scale failures in desktop work announce themselves through permission sprawl and platform drift well before the hard boundary, so leading indicators buy the response time that hard limits cannot
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: limits are read as targets to approach, platform-specific divergence is discovered at release, or an auto-updater rollout proceeds because no one owned the escalation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the statement bounds this planning reference and does not define scaling architecture for the application itself, which needs its own capacity and distribution design
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add leading approach indicators and pre-crossing actions for each stated boundary
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that scale limits protect a workflow only when paired with early-warning signals; a boundary detected at the boundary has already been crossed

## Section 026: Evidence Boundary Notes
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed notes define the three labels correctly but give no application rules, what to do when a statement mixes origins, how labels survive quoting, or which label governs the many unrefreshed external claims above
- **supporting_reason:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because evidence boundaries exist to keep confidence calibrated downstream, and labels that live only in one closing section are shed the moment a sentence is quoted into a prompt or packet
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a section-level label is stretched over claims of mixed origin, unrefreshed external rows are cited as external fact, or the inference label becomes a dumping ground that stops distinguishing reasoned synthesis from guesswork
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the notes govern labeling within this reference and its reuses, and do not rank source quality, which the hierarchy and research map handle
- **revision_decision:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add claim-level application rules, mixed-origin splitting, and retrieval-dated requirements for the external label
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that evidence labels are a chain of custody; the chain's strength is set at the weakest reuse, not at the section where the labels were first defined

- **current_section_observation:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to label at the claim level rather than the section level, split mixed statements into separately labeled clauses, and downgrade any external claim without a dated retrieval record to inference until refreshed

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 026 "Evidence Boundary Notes", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a section-level label is stretched over claims of mixed origin, unrefreshed external rows are cited as external fact, or the inference label becomes a dumping ground that stops distinguishing reasoned synthesis from guesswork
